class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.troyny.gov/">www.troyny.gov</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Troy</b> is a <a href="/wiki/City_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="City (New York)">city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> and the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_County,_New_York" title="Rensselaer County, New York">Rensselaer County</a>. The city is located on the western edge of Rensselaer County and on the eastern bank of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>. Troy has close ties to the nearby cities of <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schenectady,_New_York" title="Schenectady, New York">Schenectady</a>, forming a region popularly called the <a href="/wiki/Capital_District,_New_York" title="Capital District, New York">Capital District</a>. The city is one of the three major centers for the Albany Metropolitan Statistical Area (MSA), which has a population of 1,170,483. At the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Census 2010">2010 census</a>, the population of Troy was 50,129. Troy\'s motto is <i>Ilium fuit. Troja est</i>, which means "Ilium was, Troy is".<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Troy is home to <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>, the oldest private engineering and technical university in the USA, founded in 1824. Due to the confluence of major waterways and a geography that supported water power, the American industrial revolution took hold in this area making Troy reputedly the fourth wealthiest city in America around the turn of the 20th century. Troy, therefore, is noted for a wealth of Victorian architecture downtown and elaborate private homes in various neighborhoods. Several churches boast a concentrated collection of stained glass windows by Louis Comfort Tiffany. Troy is also home to the world renowned "<a href="/wiki/Troy_Savings_Bank_Music_Hall" title="Troy Savings Bank Music Hall">Troy Music Hall</a>", officially, the "Troy Savings Bank Music Hall" dating from the 1870s, which is said to have superb acoustics in a combination of restored and well preserved performance space.\n</p><p>The area had long been occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Mahican" title="Mahican">Mahican</a> <a href="/wiki/Indian_tribe" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian tribe">Indian tribe</a>, but Dutch settlement began in the mid 17th century. The <a href="/wiki/Patroon" title="Patroon">patroon</a> <a href="/wiki/Kiliaen_van_Rensselaer_(Dutch_merchant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiliaen van Rensselaer (Dutch merchant)">Kiliaen van Rensselaer</a> called the region Pafraets Dael, after his mother. The Dutch colony was conquered by the English in 1664, and in 1707 Derick Van der Heyden purchased a farm near today\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_Troy_Historic_District" title="Central Troy Historic District">downtown area</a>. In 1771, Abraham Lansing had his farm in today\'s <a href="/wiki/Lansingburgh,_New_York" title="Lansingburgh, New York">Lansingburgh</a> laid out into lots. Sixteen years later, Van der Heyden\'s grandson Jacob had his extensive holdings surveyed and laid out into lots, naming the new village Vanderheyden.\n</p><p>In 1789, Troy adopted its present name following a vote of the people. Troy was incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Town_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Town (New York)">town</a> two years later and extended east across the county to the <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> line, including <a href="/wiki/Petersburgh,_New_York" title="Petersburgh, New York">Petersburgh</a>. In 1796, Troy became a <a href="/wiki/Village_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Village (New York)">village</a> and in 1816, it became a city. Lansingburgh, to the north, became part of Troy in 1900.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Geography"><span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Architecture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Executive_branch"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Executive branch</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10"><a href="#Electoral_history"><span class="tocnumber">7.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Electoral history</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Legislative_branch"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Legislative branch</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Political_boundaries"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Political boundaries</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a href="#City_Council_districts"><span class="tocnumber">7.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">City Council districts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14"><a href="#New_York_State_Senate_districts"><span class="tocnumber">7.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">New York State Senate districts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#New_York_State_Assembly_districts"><span class="tocnumber">7.3.3</span> <span class="toctext">New York State Assembly districts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#Other_districts"><span class="tocnumber">7.3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Other districts</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Notable_landmarks"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Notable landmarks</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Notable_people"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Rensselaer_County_histories"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">Rensselaer County histories</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Troy_histories"><span class="tocnumber">12.2</span> <span class="toctext">Troy histories</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Troy,_New_York" title="History of Troy, New York">History of Troy, New York</a></div>\n<p>Prior to the arrival of Europeans, the <a href="/wiki/Mohican" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohican">Mohican Indians</a> had a number of settlements along the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> near the confluence with the <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_River" title="Mohawk River">Mohawk River</a>. The land comprising the Poesten Kill and Wynants Kill areas were owned by two Mohican groups. The land around the Poesten Kill was owned by <i>Skiwias</i> and was called <i>Panhooseck</i>. The area around the Wynants Kill, was known as <i>Paanpack</i>, was owned by <i>Peyhaunet</i>. The land between the creeks, which makes up most of <a href="/wiki/Central_Troy_Historic_District" title="Central Troy Historic District">downtown</a> and South Troy, was owned by <i>Annape</i>. South of the Wynants Kill and into present-day <a href="/wiki/North_Greenbush,_New_York" title="North Greenbush, New York">North Greenbush</a>, the land was owned by <i>Pachquolapiet</i>. These parcels of land were sold to the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> between 1630 and 1657 and each purchase was overseen and signed by Skiwias, the <a href="/wiki/Sachem" title="Sachem">sachem</a> at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-rittner27_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rittner27-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In total, more than 75 individual Mohicans were involved in deed signings in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-rittner22_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rittner22-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The site of the city was a part of <a href="/wiki/Rensselaerswyck" class="mw-redirect" title="Rensselaerswyck">Rensselaerswyck</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Patroonship" class="mw-redirect" title="Patroonship">patroonship</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Kiliaen_van_Rensselaer_(Dutch_merchant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiliaen van Rensselaer (Dutch merchant)">Kiliaen van Rensselaer</a>. Dirck Van der Heyden was one of the first settlers. In 1707, he purchased a farm of 65 acres (26&#160;ha), which in 1787 was laid out as a village.\n</p><p>An early local legend that a Dutch girl had been kidnapped by an Indian male who did not want her to marry someone else gained some credence when two skeletons were found in a cave under Poestenkill Falls  in the 1950s. One skeleton was female and Caucasian with an iron ring. The other was Native-American and male.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name Troy (after the legendary city of <a href="/wiki/Troy" title="Troy">Troy</a>, made famous in <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Iliad" title="Iliad">Iliad</a></i>) was adopted in 1789 before which it had been known as Ashley\'s Ferry, and the region was formed into the Town of Troy in 1791 from part of the <a href="/wiki/Manor_of_Rensselaerswyck" title="Manor of Rensselaerswyck">Manor of Rensselaerswyck</a>. The township included <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_New_York" title="Brunswick, New York">Brunswick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grafton,_New_York" title="Grafton, New York">Grafton</a>. Troy became a village in 1801 and was chartered as a city in 1816. In 1900, the city of Lansingburgh was merged into Troy. In the post-Revolutionary War years, as central New York was first settled, there was a strong trend to classical names, and Troy\'s naming fits the same pattern as the New York cities of Syracuse, Rome, Utica, Ithaca, or the towns of Sempronius, Manlius, or dozens of other classically named towns to the west of Troy.\n</p><p>Northern and Western New York was a theater of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, and militia and regular army forces were led by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Van_Rensselaer_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Van Rensselaer III">Stephen Van Rensselaer</a> of Troy. Quartermaster supplies were shipped through Troy. A local butcher and meat-packer named <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wilson" title="Samuel Wilson">Samuel Wilson</a> supplied the military, and, according to an unprovable legend, barrels stamped "U.S." were jokingly taken by the troops to stand for "<a href="/wiki/Uncle_Sam" title="Uncle Sam">Uncle Sam</a>" meaning Wilson. Troy has since claimed to be the historical home of Uncle Sam.\n</p><p>Through much of the 19th and into the early 20th century, Troy was not only one of the most prosperous cities in New York State, but one of the most prosperous cities in the entire country. Prior to its rise as an industrial center, Troy was the transshipment point for meat and vegetables from Vermont, which were sent by the Hudson River to New York City. The Federal Dam at Troy is the head of the tides in the Hudson River and Hudson River sloops and steamboats plied the river on a regular basis. This trade was vastly increased after the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a>, with its eastern terminus directly across the Hudson from Troy at <a href="/wiki/Cohoes,_New_York" title="Cohoes, New York">Cohoes</a> in 1825.\n</p><p>Troy\'s one-time great wealth was produced in the steel industry, with the first American <a href="/wiki/Bessemer_process" title="Bessemer process">Bessemer converter</a> erected on the Wyantskill, a stream with a falls in a small valley at the south end of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The industry first used charcoal and iron ore from the Adirondacks. Later on, ore and coal from the Midwest was shipped on the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a> to Troy, and there processed before being sent on down the Hudson to New York City. The iron and steel was also used by the extensive federal arsenal across the Hudson at <a href="/wiki/Watervliet,_New_York" title="Watervliet, New York">Watervliet, New York</a>, then called West Troy. After the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, the steel production industry moved west to be closer to raw materials. The presence of iron and steel also made it possible for Troy to be an early site in the development of iron storefronts and steel structural supports in architecture, and there are some significant early examples still in the city.\n</p><p>The initial emphasis on heavier industry later spawned a wide variety of highly engineered mechanical and scientific equipment. Troy was the home of <a href="/wiki/Gurley_Precision_Instruments" title="Gurley Precision Instruments">W. &amp; L. E. Gurley, Co.</a>, makers of precision instruments. Gurley\'s <a href="/wiki/Theodolite" title="Theodolite">theodolites</a> were used to survey much of the American West after the Civil War and were highly regarded until laser and digital technology eclipsed the telescope and compass technology in the 1970s. Bells manufactured by Troy\'s <a href="/wiki/Meneely_Bell_Foundry" title="Meneely Bell Foundry">Meneely Bell Company</a> ring all over the world. And Troy was also home to a manufacturer of racing shells that used impregnated paper in a process that presaged the later use of fiberglass, Kevlar and carbon fiber composites.\n</p><p>This scientific and technical proficiency was supported by the presence of <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>, or RPI, one of the highest-ranked engineering schools in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> RPI was originally sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Van_Rensselaer_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Van Rensselaer III">Stephen Van Rensselaer</a>, one of the most prominent members of that family. RPI was founded in 1824, and eventually absorbed the campus of the short-lived, liberal arts-based <a href="/wiki/Troy_University_(New_York)" title="Troy University (New York)">Troy University</a>, which closed in 1862 during the Civil War. Rensselaer founded RPI for the "application of science to the common purposes of life", and it is the oldest technological university in the English-speaking world.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The institute is known for its success in the transfer of technology from the laboratory to the marketplace.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 23, 1823, <i>The Troy Sentinel</i> was the first publisher of the world-famous Christmas poem "<a href="/wiki/A_Visit_from_St._Nicholas" title="A Visit from St. Nicholas">A Visit from St. Nicholas</a>" (also known as "The Night Before Christmas" or "Twas the Night Before Christmas"). The poem was published anonymously. Its author has long been believed to have been <a href="/wiki/Clement_Clarke_Moore" title="Clement Clarke Moore">Clement Clarke Moore</a>, but its author is now regarded by a few to have been <a href="/wiki/Henry_Livingston,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Livingston, Jr.">Henry Livingston, Jr.</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Troy was an early home of professional baseball, and was the host of two major league teams. The first team to call Troy home was the <a href="/wiki/Troy_Haymakers" title="Troy Haymakers">Troy Haymakers</a>, a <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Professional_Base_Ball_Players" title="National Association of Professional Base Ball Players">National Association</a> team in 1871 and 1872. One of their major players was <a href="/wiki/Bill_Craver" title="Bill Craver">Williams H. "Bill" Craver</a>, a noted catcher and Civil War veteran, who also managed the team. Their last manager was <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wood" title="Jimmy Wood">Jimmy Wood</a>, reckoned the first Canadian in professional baseball. The Troy Haymakers folded, and Troy had no team for seven seasons. Then, for four seasons, 1879 to 1882, Troy was home to the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> <a href="/wiki/Troy_Trojans_(MLB_team)" title="Troy Trojans (MLB team)">Troy Trojans</a>. The Trojans were not competitive in the league, but they did have the biggest hitter in professional baseball, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.baseball-almanac.com/teams/troy.shtml">Dan Brouthers.</a>\n</p><p>Troy has been nearly destroyed by fire three times. The Great Troy fire of 1862 burnt the W. &amp; L. E. Gurley, Co. factory, which was later that year replaced by the new <a href="/wiki/W._%26_L._E._Gurley_Building" title="W. &amp; L. E. Gurley Building">W. &amp; L. E. Gurley Building</a>, now a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmark</a>: Gurley &amp; Sons remains a worldwide leader in precision instrumentation.\n</p><p>In 1892, Robert Ross, a poll watcher, was shot dead (and his brother wounded) by operatives of Mayor Edward Murphy, later a U.S. Senator, after uncovering a man committing voter fraud. The convicted murderer, Bartholomew "Bat" Shea, was executed in 1896, although another man, John McGough, later boasted that he had actually been the shooter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1900 Troy annexed <a href="/wiki/Lansingburgh,_New_York" title="Lansingburgh, New York">Lansingburgh</a>, a former town and village whose standing dates back prior to the War of Independence, in Rensselaer County. Lansingburgh is thus often referred to as "North Troy". However, prior to the annexation, that portion of Troy north of Division Street was called North Troy and the neighborhood south of Washington Park is referred to as South Troy. To avoid confusion with streets in Troy following the annexation, Lansingburgh\'s numbered streets were renamed: its 1st Street, 2nd Street, 3rd Street, etc., became North Troy\'s 101st Street, 102nd Street, 103rd Street, etc. Lansingburgh was home to the <a href="/wiki/Lansingburgh_Academy" title="Lansingburgh Academy">Lansingburgh Academy</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg/220px-Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg" width="220" height="86" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg/330px-Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg/440px-Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leyendecker_arrow_color_1907.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration for Arrow Collar, 1907. J.C. Leyendecker.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg/220px-Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg/330px-Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg/440px-Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Troy_NY_Union_Depot_pre1911img024.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Station_(Troy,_New_York)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Union Station (Troy, New York) (page does not exist)">Troy\'s Union Depot</a> c. 1900</div></div></div>\n<p>In addition to the strong presence of the early American steel industry, Troy was also a manufacturing center for shirts, shirtwaists, collars and cuffs. In 1825, a local resident <a href="/wiki/False-collar" class="mw-redirect" title="False-collar">Hannah Lord Montague</a>, was tired of cleaning her blacksmith husband\'s shirts. She cut off the collars of her husband\'s shirts, since only the collar was soiled, bound the edges and attached strings to hold them in place. (This also allowed the collars and cuffs to be starched separately.) Montague\'s idea caught on, and changed the fashion for American men\'s dress for a century. Her patented collars and cuffs were first manufactured by Maullin &amp; Blanchard, which eventually was absorbed by <a href="/wiki/The_Arrow_Collar_Man" title="The Arrow Collar Man">Cluett, Peabody &amp; Company</a>. Cluett\'s "Arrow shirts" are still worn by men across the country.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.arrowshirt.com/heritage.aspx">[1]</a> The large labor force required by the shirt manufacturing industry also produced in 1864 the nation\'s first female <a href="/wiki/Labor_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor union">labor union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collar_Laundry_Union" title="Collar Laundry Union">Collar Laundry Union</a>, founded in Troy by <a href="/wiki/Kate_Mullany" title="Kate Mullany">Kate Mullany</a>. On February 23, 1864, 300 members of the union went on strike. After six days, the laundry owners gave in to their demands and raised wages 25%. There were further developments in the industry, when, in 1933, Sanford Cluett invented a process he called <a href="/wiki/Sanforization" title="Sanforization">Sanforization</a>, a process that shrinks <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">fabrics</a> thoroughly and permanently. Cluett, Peabody\'s last main plant in Troy was closed in the 1980s, but the industrial output of the plant had long been transferred to facilities in the South.\n</p><p>When the iron and steel industry moved west to Pennsylvania and beyond, and with a similar downturn in the collar industry, Troy\'s prosperity began to fade. After the passage of <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">Prohibition</a>, and given the strict control of <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a> by the O\'Connell political machine, Troy became a way station for an <a href="/wiki/Rum-running" title="Rum-running">illegal alcohol trade</a> from Canada to New York City. Likewise, the stricter control of morality laws in the neighboring <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> states encouraged the development of openly operating speakeasies and brothels in Troy. Gangsters such as "<a href="/wiki/Legs_Diamond" title="Legs Diamond">Legs Diamond</a>" conducted their business in Troy, giving the city a somewhat colorful reputation through World War II. A few of the buildings from that era have since been converted to fine restaurants, such as the former Old Daly Inn.\n</p><p>Like many old industrial cities, Troy has had to deal with not only the loss of its manufacturing base, but a loss of population and wealth to <a href="/wiki/Suburbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Suburbs">suburbs</a> and other parts of the country. This led to dilapidation and disinvestment, until later efforts were made to preserve Troy\'s architectural and cultural past.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">Kurt Vonnegut</a> lived in Troy and the area, and many of his novels include mentions of "Ilium" (an alternate name for Troy) or surrounding locations. Vonnegut wrote <a href="/wiki/Player_Piano_(novel)" title="Player Piano (novel)"><i>Player Piano</i></a> in 1952, based on his experiences working as a <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> writer at nearby <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>. His 1963 novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Cat%27s_Cradle_(novel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cat&#39;s Cradle (novel)">Cat\'s Cradle</a></i>, was written in the city and is set in Ilium. His recurring main character, Kilgore Trout, is a resident of <a href="/wiki/Cohoes,_New_York" title="Cohoes, New York">Cohoes</a>, just across the Hudson River from Troy.\n</p><p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Troy is updating its citywide comprehensive plan for the first time in more than 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_Union_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Union-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The two-year process is known as "Realize Troy" and was initiated by the Troy Redevelopment Foundation (with members from the Emma Willard School, <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Sage_College" title="Russell Sage College">Russell Sage College</a> and St. Peter\'s Health Partners). Urban Strategies Inc. (Toronto) is planning Troy\'s redevelopment.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_Union_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Union-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1208px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg" class="image" title="Troy, as viewed from across the Hudson River looking east, circa 1909"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg/1200px-Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg" width="1200" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg/1800px-Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg/2400px-Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3776" data-file-height="632" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Troy_NY_1909_LOC_6a14121u.jpg" title="File:Troy NY 1909 LOC 6a14121u.jpg"> </a></div>Troy, as viewed from across the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> looking east, <i><a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">circa</a></i> 1909</div>\n</div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_Troy_map_2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/City_of_Troy_map_2.svg/220px-City_of_Troy_map_2.svg.png" width="220" height="459" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/City_of_Troy_map_2.svg/330px-City_of_Troy_map_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/City_of_Troy_map_2.svg/440px-City_of_Troy_map_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="230" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_of_Troy_map_2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the neighborhoods of Troy</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, the city has a total area of 11.0 square miles (28&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), of which 10.4 square miles (27&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 0.6 square miles (1.6&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) (5.44%) is water.\n</p><p>Troy is located several miles north of Albany near the junction of the Erie and Champlain canals, via the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> and is the terminus of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Barge_Canal" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Barge Canal">New York Barge Canal</a>. It is the distributing center for a large area.<sup id="cite_ref-Breuer_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Breuer-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is on the central part of the western border of Rensselaer County. The Hudson River makes up the western border of the city and the county\'s border with Albany County. The city borders within Rensselaer County, <a href="/wiki/Schaghticoke,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Schaghticoke, New York">Schaghticoke</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_New_York" title="Brunswick, New York">Brunswick</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/North_Greenbush,_New_York" title="North Greenbush, New York">North Greenbush</a> to the south; to the west the city borders the Albany County town of <a href="/wiki/Colonie,_New_York" title="Colonie, New York">Colonie</a>, the villages of <a href="/wiki/Menands,_New_York" title="Menands, New York">Menands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_Island,_New_York" title="Green Island, New York">Green Island</a>, and the cities of <a href="/wiki/Watervliet,_New_York" title="Watervliet, New York">Watervliet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cohoes,_New_York" title="Cohoes, New York">Cohoes</a>. To the northwest Troy borders the Saratoga County village of <a href="/wiki/Waterford_(village),_New_York" title="Waterford (village), New York">Waterford</a> within the town of <a href="/wiki/Waterford,_New_York" title="Waterford, New York">Waterford</a>\n</p><p>The western edge of the city is flat along the river, and then steeply slopes to higher terrain to the east. The average elevation is 50 feet, with the highest elevation being 500 feet in the eastern part of the city. The city is longer than it is wide, with the southern part wider than the northern section of the city (the formerly separate city of <a href="/wiki/Lansingburgh,_New_York" title="Lansingburgh, New York">Lansingburgh</a>). Several <a href="/wiki/Kill_(body_of_water)" title="Kill (body of water)">kills</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch (language)">Dutch</a> for creek) pass through Troy and empty into the Hudson. The Poesten Kill and Wynants Kill are the two largest and both have several small lakes and waterfalls along their routes in the city. There are several lakes and reservoirs within the city including Ida Lake, Burden Pond, Lansingburgh Reservoir, Bradley Lake, Smarts Pond and Wright Lake.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0 0 1em 1em; text-align:right">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" class="navbox-title" style="padding-right:3px; padding-left:3px; font-size:110%; text-align:center">Historical population\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:95%">\n<th style="text-align:center; text-align: center;">\xe2\x88\x9210.0%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b><a href="/wiki/1990_United_States_Census" title="1990 United States Census">1990</a></b></td><td style="padding-left:8px;">54,269</td><td style="font-size:85%"></td><td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">2.0%</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:center"><b>Est. 2016</b></td><td style="padding-left:8px;">49,702</td><td style="font-size:85%"><sup id="cite_ref-USCensusEst2016_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCensusEst2016-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td><td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\xe2\x88\x920.9%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">U.S. Decennial Census<sup id="cite_ref-DecennialCensus_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DecennialCensus-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>At the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a>, there were 50,129 people, 20,121 households and 10,947 families residing in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-quickfacts_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quickfacts-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The population density was 4,840.1 per square mile. There were 23,474 housing units. The racial makeup of the city was 69.7% non-Hispanic <a href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 16.4% <a href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 0.3% <a href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 3.4% <a href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0% <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, and 4.1% from two or more races. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 7.9% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-quickfacts_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quickfacts-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The median household income in 2013 was $37,805 (NYS average of $57,369), and the median family income was $47,827 (NYS average of $70,485). The median per capita income for the city was $20,872 (NYS average of $32,514). About 27.3% of the population were living in poverty as of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-citydata_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citydata-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(February 2009)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Troy is known as the "Collar City" due to its history in shirt, collar, and other textile production. At one point Troy was also the second largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a> in the country, surpassed only by the city of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania</a>.\n</p><p>The Rensselaer School, which later became <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a> (RPI), was founded in 1824 with funding from <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Van_Rensselaer" title="Stephen Van Rensselaer">Stephen Van Rensselaer</a>, a descendant of the founding patroon, Kiliaen. In 1821, <a href="/wiki/Emma_Willard" title="Emma Willard">Emma Willard</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Troy_Female_Seminary" class="mw-redirect" title="Troy Female Seminary">Troy Female Seminary</a>. It was renamed <a href="/wiki/Emma_Willard_School" title="Emma Willard School">Emma Willard School</a> in 1895. The former Female Seminary was later reopened (1916) as <a href="/wiki/Russell_Sage_College" title="Russell Sage College">Russell Sage College</a>. All of these institutions still exist today.\n</p><p>Troy, like many older industrial cities, has been battered by <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization" title="Deindustrialization">industrial decline</a> and the migration of jobs to the suburbs. Nevertheless, the presence of <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a> is helping Troy develop a small high-technology sector, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Video_game_development" title="Video game development">video game development</a>. The downtown core also has a smattering of advertising and architecture firms, and other creative businesses attracted by the area\'s distinctive architecture. RPI is the city\'s largest private employer.\n</p><p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/Russell_Sage_College" title="Russell Sage College">Russell Sage College</a> (a comprehensive college for women), Troy is also home to the 10,000-student <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley_Community_College" title="Hudson Valley Community College">Hudson Valley Community College</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a> system), three private high schools: La Salle Institute (Catholic military-style), <a href="/wiki/Emma_Willard_School" title="Emma Willard School">Emma Willard School</a> (America\'s first girl\'s high school and a high-academic boarding and day school) and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Central_High_School_(Troy,_New_York)" title="Catholic Central High School (Troy, New York)">Catholic Central High School</a> (a regional Catholic high school in Lansingburg section).\n</p><p>Northeast Health is now the umbrella administration of Troy two large hospitals (Samaritan Hospital and St. Mary\'s Hospital). The city is also home to many non-profits including the many good services provided by Unity House, Joseph\'s House, numerous churches (Orthodox, Catholic, and Protestant), three synagogues, and one mosque.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(December 2011)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Troy is home to <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belle_%C3%89poque" title="Belle \xc3\x89poque">Belle \xc3\x89poque</a> <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>. The city\'s architectural achievements rate inspirational and serve its citizens, visitors and onlookers as well as posterity, with as a veritable treasure chest set in masonry exteriors, as evidenced by the sheer variety of its building\'s design vernacular, which includes specimens redolent of numerous ancient civilizations\' and later European edifice models.\nNotably, the city\'s First and Second <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolutions</a>\' decades-long innovations and successes enabled commercial and residential builders the financial means and engineering knowledgebase to express themselves in highly individualized, and most often, grand masonry buildings. That opportunity to build such wondrous structures is owed, in part, too, to the fact that two major fires had devastated much of Troy\'s earlier wooden structures, availing large tracts for re-development.\n</p><p>The Hudson and Mohawk rivers play their part, as does the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a> and its lesser tributary canal systems, and later the railroads that linked Troy to the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State" title="Empire State">Empire State</a>, New York City to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Utica,_New_York" title="Utica, New York">Utica, New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse, New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo, New York</a> and the myriad of emergent <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>\' cities in the burgeoning United States.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg" class="image"><img alt="This is a photo of the Payne Mansion( Pi Kappa Phi Fraternity House) Dining room showing a Tiffany stained glass window, built in buffet, cherry inlaid floors and the choir loft." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg/220px-Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg/330px-Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg/440px-Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4898" data-file-height="3265" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Payne_Mansion_Dining_Room.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Payne Mansion (2017)</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_buildings">Notable buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Notable buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a></li>\n<li>The Emma Willard School for Girls aka <a href="/wiki/Emma_Willard_School" title="Emma Willard School">Emma Willard School</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hart-Cluett_Mansion" title="Hart-Cluett Mansion">The Hart-Cluett Mansion</a></li>\n<li>Paine Mansion<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Russell_Sage_College" title="Russell Sage College">Russell Sage College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Troy_Public_Library" title="Troy Public Library">Troy Public Library</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley_Community_College" title="Hudson Valley Community College">Hudson Valley Community College</a></li></ul>\n<p>Natives of Troy expressed their passion for building, using the following materials, for an array of building features:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Iron: cast and structural iron works (facades, gates, railings, banisters, stairwells, rooftop crenellation, window grilles, etc.)</li>\n<li>Stone: carved hard and soft stone foundations, facades and decorative elements</li>\n<li>Glass: as well as in the vast array of ornate stained and etched glass works;</li>\n<li>Wood: fine wood work in found in many of Troy\'s buildings.</li></ul>\n<p>Tiffany and La Farge created magnificent stained-glass windows, transoms and other decorative stained-glass treatments for their customers in Troy. With many examples of intact 19th-century architecture, particularly in its <a href="/wiki/Central_Troy_Historic_District" title="Central Troy Historic District">Central Troy Historic District</a>, this has helped to lure several major movies to film in Troy, including <i><a href="/wiki/Ironweed_(film)" title="Ironweed (film)">Ironweed</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Age_of_Innocence_(1993_film)" title="The Age of Innocence (1993 film)">The Age of Innocence</a> (Filmed partially in the Paine mansion)</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Scent_of_a_Woman_(1992_film)" title="Scent of a Woman (1992 film)">Scent of a Woman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bostonians_(film)" title="The Bostonians (film)">The Bostonians</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emperor%27s_Club" title="The Emperor&#39;s Club">The Emperor\'s Club</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Time_Machine_(2002_film)" title="The Time Machine (2002 film)">The Time Machine</a>.</i> There are many buildings in a state of disrepair, but community groups and investors are restoring many of them.\n</p><p>Troy\'s downtown historic landmarks include Frear\'s Troy Cash Bazaar, constructed on a steel infrastructure clad in ornately carved white marble; the <a href="/wiki/Corinthian_order" title="Corinthian order">Corinthian</a> Courthouse that is constructed of gray granite; the Troy Public Library, built in an elaborate Venetian palazzo style with high-relief carved white marble; the Troy Savings Bank Music Hall, designed in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Empire_(architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Empire (architecture)">Second Empire</a> style, with a recital hall with highly regarded acoustic properties. There is a rich collection of <a href="/wiki/American_colonial_architecture" title="American colonial architecture">Colonial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_architecture" title="Federal architecture">Federal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italianate" class="mw-redirect" title="Italianate">Italianate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Empire_(architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Empire (architecture)">Second Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Revival">Greek Revival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian Revival">Egyptian Revival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic Revival">Gothic Revival</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Romantic_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Romantic period">Romantic period</a> townhouses surrounding the immediate downtown. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081230160113/http://www.rchsonline.org/ar_hc.htm">Hart-Cluett Mansion</a> displays a Federal facade executed in white marble, quarried in <a href="/wiki/Tuckahoe,_Westchester_County,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuckahoe, Westchester County, New York">Tuckahoe, New York</a>. Often with foundations of <a href="/wiki/Rustication_(architecture)" title="Rustication (architecture)">rusticated</a> granite block. Medina sandstone, a deep mud-red color, from <a href="/wiki/Medina,_New_York" title="Medina, New York">Medina, New York</a>, was also used.\n</p><p>As with many American cities, several city blocks in downtown Troy were razed during the 1970s as a part of an attempted <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a> plan, which was never successfully executed, leaving still vacant areas in the vicinity of Federal Street. Today, however, there have since been much more successful efforts to save the remaining historic downtown structures.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG/220px-RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG/330px-RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG/440px-RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3110" data-file-height="2188" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RiverStreetTroyNY.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northern River Street</div></div></div>\n<p>Part of this effort has been the arrival of the "Antique District" on River Street downtown. Cafes and art galleries are calling the area home. As home to many art, literature, and music lovers, the city hosts many free shows during the summer, on River Street, in parks, and in cafes and coffee shops. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.troymarket.org/">Troy Farmer\'s Market</a> is a popular event since 2000 that occurs every Saturday on River Street during the summer, or in the Atrium of downtown Troy during the winter. The market offers over 70 local vendors offering a variety of goods.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_events">Recurring events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li>Troy Flag Day Parade \xe2\x80\x93 The Troy Flag Day Parade was the largest one to honor the American flag in the U.S., taking place in early June. It started in 1967 and ended in 2017, after 51 years.</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.downtowntroy.org/troy-river-fest/">Troy River Fest</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Annual, family-oriented arts/crafts and music festival held in June. Showcasing carefully curated, locally crafted hand-made goods and local cuisine in an open-air bazaar situated in the scenic, historic downtown district.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Uncle Sam Parade \xe2\x80\x93 Held in proximity to <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Wilson" title="Samuel Wilson">Samuel Wilson</a>\'s birthday (mid-September)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bakerloo.org">Bakerloo Theatre Project</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Classical summer theatre<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.victorianstroll.com">The Victorian Stroll</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Annual holiday event (December)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.troyturkeytrot.com">Troy Turkey Trot</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Annual <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Thanksgiving Day">Thanksgiving Day</a> Run; the oldest race in the Capital District.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.enchantedtroy.com">"The Enchanted City"</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Steampunk" title="Steampunk">Steampunk</a> festival set in the historic streets of downtown Troy, (August, was previously in October)<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.downtowntroy.org/troy-night-out/">Troy Night Out</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Last Friday of every month. Arts and cultural event that regularly draws thousands people onto the streets of Downtown Troy. Attendees enjoy countless art events, music venues, fine restaurants and unique boutiques of all varieties.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.downtowntroy.org/rockin-on-the-river/">Rockin\' on the River</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Every Wednesday evening from June 18 through August 27, the Downtown Troy Business Improvement District and the City of Troy present this free, outdoor concert series"<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.downtowntroy.org/troy-pig-out/">Troy Pig Out</a> \xe2\x80\x93 One of the most loved summertime events in the Capital Region, the Troy Pig Out is a full day of fun where culinary competitors duke it out for best BBQ, and people flock to Riverfront park to taste some of the area\xe2\x80\x99s best food.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.downtowntroy.org/chowder-fest/">Chowderfest</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Chowder tasting throughout downtown Troy. Numerous local retailers participate in the day\'s activities with a citywide sidewalk sale. It\'s a full day of fall food, live music, and family fun!<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>In 2009, Troy ranked #15 on <i><a href="/wiki/Newsmax" title="Newsmax">Newsmax</a></i> magazine\'s list of the "Top 25 Most Uniquely American Cities and Towns", a piece written by current <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> travel editor <a href="/wiki/Peter_Greenberg" title="Peter Greenberg">Peter Greenberg</a>. In determining his ranking, Greenberg cited Troy\'s Flag Day Parade and called the city a "great example of American spirit".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Troy_City_Council.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Troy_City_Council.JPG/220px-Troy_City_Council.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Troy_City_Council.JPG/330px-Troy_City_Council.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Troy_City_Council.JPG/440px-Troy_City_Council.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Troy_City_Council.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>City Council meeting in the former City Hall on River Street</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Executive branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The executive branch consists of a mayor who serves as the chief executive officer of the city. The mayor is responsible for the proper administration of all city affairs placed in his/her charge as empowered by the city charter. The mayor enforces the laws of New York State as well as all local laws and ordinances passed by the city council. She or he exercises control over all executive departments of the city government, including the Departments of Finance, Law, Public Safety, Public Works, Public Utilities, and Parks and Recreation.\n</p><p>The mayor\'s term of office is four years, and an incumbent is prohibited from serving for more than two consecutive terms (eight years).\n</p><p>The current mayor of Troy is Patrick Madden (D), who is serving his first term, having been elected on November 3, 2015.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_history">Electoral history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Electoral history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Results from the last six mayoral elections (an asterisk indicates the incumbent):\n</p>\n<ul><li>November 3, 2015 \xe2\x80\x93 Patrick Madden (D) defeated Jim Gordon (R)</li>\n<li>November 8, 2011 \xe2\x80\x93 Lou Rosamilia (D, WF) defeated Carmella Mantello (R, I, C)</li>\n<li>November 6, 2007 \xe2\x80\x93 Harry Tutunjian *(R, I, C) defeated James Conroy (D), Elda Abate (TPP)</li>\n<li>November 4, 2003 \xe2\x80\x93 Harry Tutunjian (R, I, C) defeated Frank LaPosta (D)</li>\n<li>November 2, 1999 \xe2\x80\x93 Mark Pattison *(D, L, W) defeated Carmella Mantello (R, I, C)</li>\n<li>November 7, 1995 \xe2\x80\x93 Mark Pattison (D, C) defeated Kathleen Jimino (R, RtL, Fre), Michael Petruska (I, W), Michael Rourke (L)</li>\n<li>prior to the November 1995 election, a <a href="/wiki/Council%E2%80%93manager_government" title="Council\xe2\x80\x93manager government">city-manager</a> form of government was utilized</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Troy\'s legislative branch consists of a city council composed of seven elected members: one at-large member who represents the entire city and acts as City Council President, and six district members who represent each of the six districts of Troy. Currently, there are 4 Democrats and 3 Republicans.\n</p><p>Each council member serves a two-year term and an incumbent is prohibited from serving for more than four consecutive terms (eight years).\n</p><p>The council meets on the first Thursday of every month at 7:00&#160;pm in the City Hall council chambers. All meetings are open to the public and include a public forum period held before official business where residents can address the council on all matters directly pertaining to city government.\n</p><p>The current Troy City Council took office on January 1, 2018, and will serve until December 31, 2019. The members are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Carmella Mantello (R \xe2\x80\x93 At-Large; President)</li>\n<li>Jim Gulli (R \xe2\x80\x93 District 1)</li>\n<li>Mark McGrath (R \xe2\x80\x93 District 2)</li>\n<li>Coleen Murtagh Paratore (D \xe2\x80\x93 District 3)</li>\n<li>Anasha Cummings (D \xe2\x80\x93 District 4; President Pro Tempore)</li>\n<li>David Bissember (D \xe2\x80\x93 District 5)</li>\n<li>TJ Kennedy (D \xe2\x80\x93 District 6)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_boundaries">Political boundaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political boundaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The City of Troy is divided into thirty (30) election districts, also known as EDs. An ED is the finest granularity political district that can be used, from which all other political districts are formed.\n</p><p>Other political districts that make use of these EDs include City Council Districts, County Legislative Districts, State Assembly Districts, State Senate Districts, and U.S. Congressional Districts.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Council_districts">City Council districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: City Council districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The 30 EDs are grouped into six Council Districts, as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Council District 1: ED1\xe2\x80\x93ED6</li>\n<li>Council District 2: ED7\xe2\x80\x93ED10</li>\n<li>Council District 3: ED11\xe2\x80\x93ED15</li>\n<li>Council District 4: ED16\xe2\x80\x93ED18</li>\n<li>Council District 5: ED19\xe2\x80\x93ED24</li>\n<li>Council District 6: ED25\xe2\x80\x93ED30</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_State_Senate_districts">New York State Senate districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: New York State Senate districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Two <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Senate" title="New York State Senate">New York State Senate</a> Districts, the 43rd and the 44th, each share a portion of their total areas with groups of EDs in Troy as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nysenate.gov/district/43">Senate District 43</a>: ED1\xe2\x80\x93ED7</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nysenate.gov/district/44">Senate District 44</a>: ED8\xe2\x80\x93ED30</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_State_Assembly_districts">New York State Assembly districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: New York State Assembly districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Two <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Assembly" title="New York State Assembly">New York State Assembly</a> Districts, the 107th and the 108th, each share a portion of their total areas with groups of EDs in Troy as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.assembly.state.ny.us/mem/?ad=107&amp;sh=map">Assembly District 107</a>: ED1\xe2\x80\x93ED8, ED12\xe2\x80\x93ED15, ED23</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.assembly.state.ny.us/mem/?ad=108&amp;sh=map">Assembly District 108</a>: ED9\xe2\x80\x93ED11, ED16\xe2\x80\x93ED22, ED24\xe2\x80\x93ED30</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_districts">Other districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>All other political districts that exist in Troy consist of the entire city \xe2\x80\x94 all 30 EDs:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="New York&#39;s 20th congressional district">U.S. Congressional District 20</a>: ED1\xe2\x80\x93ED30</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_County,_New_York#Government_and_politics" title="Rensselaer County, New York">Rensselaer County Legislative District 1</a>: ED1\xe2\x80\x93ED30</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_landmarks">Notable landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Troy,_New_York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notable landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TroyNYSign.JPG" class="image"><img alt=""
